────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
ARTICLE: Anti Spam Policy
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Q1: If-an-account-is-blocked-due-to-reaching-overlimit-of-spam-abuse-count-will-the-survey-in-field-gets-locked-as-well
Context: No. The survey still remains open for the respondents to take and responses are still collected. Only the account is blocked and our security team reviews the survey send-outs and accordingly they will give suggestions to avoid such situations. The reason for doing this is, if the respondents mark the survey invite as spam then the QuestionPro mailing servers get the spam hit directly and if the count increases then it might get blacklisted and this will affect the overall send-outs for other clients as well. Thus to avoid such a situation we have taken this additional step.
A: (See full answer at https://www.questionpro.com/help/anti-spam-policy/If-an-account-is-blocked-due-to-reaching-overlimit-of-spam-abuse-count-will-the-survey-in-field-gets-locked-as-well.html)
Source: https://www.questionpro.com/help/anti-spam-policy/If-an-account-is-blocked-due-to-reaching-overlimit-of-spam-abuse-count-will-the-survey-in-field-gets-locked-as-well.html

The current plan is to have a system where 5 or more soft bounces equate to a hard bounce.
A: (See full answer at https://www.questionpro.com/help/email-delivery-faq/Do-weve-any-expected-ETA-on-segregating-the-soft--hard-bounces.html)
Source: https://www.questionpro.com/help/email-delivery-faq/Do-weve-any-expected-ETA-on-segregating-the-soft--hard-bounces.html

Q2: How-is-QuestionPro-handling-email-bounces
Context: The help article doesn’t mention MX anywhere on it. MX records are used to set up domains for receiving emails, they tell the internet which server to send mail to. More info here: https://www.cloudflare.com/en-gb/learning/dns/dns-records/dns-mx-record/ We at our current implementation in Qualtrics & looking at the name of the record for Qualtrics the MX is used for bounces, so their system must track and do something with the returned emails. The record is only for receiving email, but it is often used by receiving mail systems to check the sender for spam too. It’s easy to send emails, often harder to have proper MX records set up to show the mailbox is a receiver too. Our main email vendor is Sendgrid, their docs for the same process regarding record setup is here: https://www.twilio.com/docs/sendgrid/ui/account-and-settings/how-to-set-up-domain-authentication How does QuestionPro intend to handle the bounces?
A: (See full answer at https://www.questionpro.com/help/email-delivery-faq/How-is-QuestionPro-handling-email-bounces.html)
Source: https://www.questionpro.com/help/email-delivery-faq/How-is-QuestionPro-handling-email-bounces.html
